<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2857882285374552591">High school all-American Neely Crenshaw was probably the best quarterback ever to play for the legendary Messina Spartans. Fifteen years have gone by since those glory days, and Neely has come home to Messina to bury Coach Eddie Rake, the man who molded the Spartans into an unbeatable football dynasty.<br /><br />Now, as Coach Rake’s “boys” sit in the bleachers waiting for the dimming</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2857882285374552591">High school all-American Neely Crenshaw was probably the best quarterback ever to play for the legendary Messina Spartans. Fifteen years have gone by since those glory days, and Neely has come home to Messina to bury Coach Eddie Rake, the man who molded the Spartans into an unbeatable football dynasty.<br /><br />Now, as Coach Rake’s “boys” sit in the bleachers waiting for the dimming field lights to signal his passing, they replay the old games, relive the old glories, and try to decide once and for all whether they love Eddie Rake – or hate him. For Neely Crenshaw, a man who must finally forgive his coach – and himself – before he can get on with his life, the stakes are especially high.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_273736800">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/273736800" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="left imgcol" title="Jane Stewart"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" alt="Jane Stewart" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/273736800?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="user" title="Jane Stewart">Jane Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13456510-bleachers" title="Audiobook " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=football-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">football-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer273736800">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8557208122042871801">It was not fun. Guys who played high school football 15 yrs ago reminisce about the past. Melancholy and sadness.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Eddie Rake was a tough, mean, high school football coach with undefeated teams for many years. He now has cancer and is expected to die any day. Guys who used to play football for him have returned to town for the coming funeral. Neely was a star quarterback in high school. His career was cut short due to a knee injury in college. Neely talks with other guys about the past</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8557208122042871801">It was not fun. Guys who played high school football 15 yrs ago reminisce about the past. Melancholy and sadness.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Eddie Rake was a tough, mean, high school football coach with undefeated teams for many years. He now has cancer and is expected to die any day. Guys who used to play football for him have returned to town for the coming funeral. Neely was a star quarterback in high school. His career was cut short due to a knee injury in college. Neely talks with other guys about the past.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />This isn’t the kind of storytelling I’m used to from Grisham. It’s not as fun. Almost everything is being “told” not shown. We listen to the guys reminisce and remember events from the past. It was interesting in a newspaper reporting kind of way. There is no excitement, suspense, or anticipation. I didn’t feel anything as I listened. I didn’t laugh or smile. At best it was ok. I felt the author may have been experimenting - trying a different style of writing.<br /><br />Some of it was about brutality and violence in football. A lot of it was sad to see what happens to football players after they no longer play. I was sad for Neely at the losses in his life. His wrecked knee. He lost the only two women he ever loved. He broke up with one of them for a stupid reason, and he regrets it. He had no desire to study and better himself after his football career was over. He’s not happy. He’s resigned to life.<br /><br />NARRATOR:<br />The author narrated his own book which was ok. It was interesting to hear his southern accent.<br /><br />DATA:	<br />Unabridged audiobook story length: 4 hrs and 22 mins. Swearing language: none that I recall. Sexual content: none. Setting: current day Messina, Mississippi. Book copyright: 2003. Genre: football fiction. Ending: sad, resigned, life goes on.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8557208122042871801">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/674412-kevin" class="left imgcol" title="Kevin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439783685p2/674412.jpg" alt="Kevin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/24843463?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 18, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/674412-kevin" class="user" title="Kevin">Kevin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24843463">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1264977753865672186">Fifteen years after swearing he would never return, Neely Crenshaw finds himself back in Messina, Texas, awaiting final word that local legend and former football coach Eddie Rake has died. When he left, Neely had become a local legend as one of the best quarterbacks in Messina High's history, but a falling out between him and the coach left him bitter and kept him away until this moment. Now, he finds himself drudging up the specters of the past with his former teammates as well as other former</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1264977753865672186">Fifteen years after swearing he would never return, Neely Crenshaw finds himself back in Messina, Texas, awaiting final word that local legend and former football coach Eddie Rake has died. When he left, Neely had become a local legend as one of the best quarterbacks in Messina High's history, but a falling out between him and the coach left him bitter and kept him away until this moment. Now, he finds himself drudging up the specters of the past with his former teammates as well as other former Rake players from other eras. This is a very painful novel to read having played high school football myself and I share many of the same feelings towards my old coach as Neely does — and as I'm sure many other former athletes do — despite the fact that I was not a star, hell I wasn't even a first stringer. In all honesty, this feels like a novelized version of what a sequel to the movie Varsity Blues would be. It's easy to tell that this story is very close to Grisham's heart and that he took the writing of this book very seriously as there are no cheesy subplots or alternate storylines to detract from the main story at hand. My only complaint was that this book was far too short. Clocking in at a mere 163 pages, this novel can be cranked out in one sitting and I felt that more could have been developed upon.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1264977753865672186">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10388860154039244649">I enjoyed , "The Bleachers". It is apparent that you have no concept of what playing a team sport requires. Those of us that have sweated and worked t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10388860154039244649">I enjoyed , "The Bleachers". It is apparent that you have no concept of what playing a team sport requires. Those of us that have sweated and worked together to pursue a joint goal understand what John Grisham is writing about in this novel. The character that you develop as a player and the relationships you make working for a common goal, overcoming similar challenges, pushing yourself outside your comfort zone, stays with you the rest of your life. Then when life throws you a curve you stand tall and attack the challenge with the same character that you displayed on the playing field. Win, Loose or Draw, you learn how to play the game of life and finish with dignity and pride. As in life you leave it all on the field, hopefully you have performed to the best of your ability. With a little bit of luck and a whole lot of hard work you can reach your goal. Sometimes it takes a person like Coach Rake to make you go the extra distance it takes to be a winner, Obviously, your not a winner and neither was your review of this fine novel.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131026610" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3010986-amanda-patterson" class="left imgcol" title="Amanda Patterson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1403880236p2/3010986.jpg" alt="Amanda Patterson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/131026610?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 16, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3010986-amanda-patterson" class="user" title="Amanda Patterson">Amanda Patterson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer131026610">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16893162504503923498">It must be boring to have to churn out a novel a year just because you’re a best-selling author. This ennui can be the only excuse for Grisham’s latest folly, Bleachers.<br /><br />What a let-down when a crime novelist who once ruled a genre turns his hand to something more literary. “An unforgettable novel,” drools the inside of the book’s jacket, which was strange as I managed to forget it immediately. I had to drag the book off the shelf to remember the main character’s name.<br /><br />Neely Crenshaw comes home for</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16893162504503923498">It must be boring to have to churn out a novel a year just because you’re a best-selling author. This ennui can be the only excuse for Grisham’s latest folly, Bleachers.<br /><br />What a let-down when a crime novelist who once ruled a genre turns his hand to something more literary. “An unforgettable novel,” drools the inside of the book’s jacket, which was strange as I managed to forget it immediately. I had to drag the book off the shelf to remember the main character’s name.<br /><br />Neely Crenshaw comes home for the burial of his school football coach, Eddie Rake. This coach was extraordinary. All of his boys remember him and the impact he made on their lives as they sit in the bleachers waiting for the stadium’s lights to dim and signal his passing.<br /><br />Things have changed in his hometown of Messina. When he was a boy, there wasn’t a place to buy an espresso. Now, everything’s available and memories blur with real time.<br />Maybe this will appeal to American football fans but I got tired of hearing of the trials of Nate and Paul and Jesse. And I nearly lost it when Coach Rakes’s funeral lasted for almost 40 pages.<br />I studied the blurb again, “this novel….is about the many ways boys become men.” Really? Hmmm. Maybe you have to be a man to get it because it left me cold. His writing is competent but his characters lack depth. The plot was missing too, but maybe it was supposed to be. Who knows? Who cares?<br /><br />I think this is one of the worst pieces of post 9/11 nonsense I’ve read. What a pity that a fine suspense author had to put all of his fans through this horrible ordeal.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16893162504503923498">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8344301271261219207">The book “Bleachers was a wonderful book to show you the positive and negatives of life when high school football is the main point. It also has a wonderful picture of what happens when you let an accident control your life. The coach showed me that there are people that you will consistently think about even with a bad situation. Everyone in life needs a person to help them with pushing yourself to get better more than we would push ourselves. If you decide to check out this book, you'll find the person who is your motivation. A weakness in this book is that there isn't really a situation in where something really exciting happens, most of it is sad. I would recommend this book to a classmate because it focuses on the outlook of life and everything that can occur. If this book was part of a series, I would continue to read it because its very interesting on how it is set up with everything happening very quickly. I would like to see how the team and everyone around would handle the whole situation. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12262645030932545426">I read this on the flight to Austin two weeks ago. Totally up my alley since it is about an iconic high school football coach and the impact he had on multiple generations of players. The former players gather in the bleachers at the school awaiting the death of the old coach as he succumbs to cancer. They slowly open up to each other sharing stories of the coach, not always glowing ones and in the memories of these players, the character of a dying man comes to life. It's an easy read as Grisham usually is, but also as is typical of his writing, there are some unexpected twists and excellent development of the characters. </span>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer231945852">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8683216062506316231">“Bleachers” is a very good and inspiriting story. It made me think what my life will be like in the future when I’m done playing football. I could relate to it in many ways and some of the things John Grisham wrote about in “Bleachers” i have actually seen or heard about in my life time.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8683216062506316231">“Bleachers” is a very good and inspiriting story. It made me think what my life will be like in the future when I’m done playing football. I could relate to it in many ways and some of the things John Grisham wrote about in “Bleachers” i have actually seen or heard about in my life time. "Bleachers" by John Grisham is about the legendary Messina Spartans football team and Coach Rake's team coming back to their home stadium and saying there last good-byes to Eddie Rake. Eddie Rake was the meanest and hardest coach throughout Spartan history but is the man who caused the Messina Spartans to be the best football team in history. While Coach Rake was slowly dying the boys got together in the bleachers and would talk about all the old games and memories they remembered and what they went through. Some memories were good and others were bad, but by the end of the night they would end up realizing what a great man and coach Eddie Rake was. He led them to many victories and state Championships and got them prepared for their future life. During the funeral, High school all-American Neely Crenshaw was probably the best quarter back to Rake and Crenshaw realized a lot once he heard some words from his old Coach. Neely Crenshaw is now a man who is all grown up and must finally forgive his coach and himself with the incidents they had in life before he can get his life back on track.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299631633" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/26225152-mario" class="left imgcol" title="Mario"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1386090180p2/26225152.jpg" alt="Mario" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1299631633?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/26225152-mario" class="user" title="Mario">Mario</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/25237531-l-allenatore" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1299631633">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14198962920231944765">Si può dire non il solito Grisham, o perlomeno non il Grisham dei legal-drama o thriller. Ma c’è anche il solito Grisham, con l’ambientazione nella provincia americana con le sue abitudini e i suoi riti settimanali. E poi c’è il football. Chi non è appassionato troverà un po’ difficile addentrarsi nelle pagine in cui descrive, anche minuziosamente, la partita che i vari personaggi ci/si raccontano e che è il fulcro attorno al quale gira la storia. È, però, soprattutto una storia sul perdono, sul</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14198962920231944765">Si può dire non il solito Grisham, o perlomeno non il Grisham dei legal-drama o thriller. Ma c’è anche il solito Grisham, con l’ambientazione nella provincia americana con le sue abitudini e i suoi riti settimanali. E poi c’è il football. Chi non è appassionato troverà un po’ difficile addentrarsi nelle pagine in cui descrive, anche minuziosamente, la partita che i vari personaggi ci/si raccontano e che è il fulcro attorno al quale gira la storia. È, però, soprattutto una storia sul perdono, sulle occasioni perdute, sul destino, sulle “sliding doors” della vita. E lungo le pagine di questo racconto, a tratti struggente, ambientato nella (immaginaria) cittadina di Messina, il protagonista troverà la forza di analizzare il suo passato, con l’aiuto dei suoi vecchi amici, interrogandosi sugli errori commessi e sul perché delle sue scelte.<br />Grisham dimostra ancora una volta, a parte la conoscenza (e, chiaramente, l’amore) per il football, di non essere uno scrittore “stereotipato”, ma capace di raccontare storie di sentimenti, di passioni e di amicizie che iniziano a consolidarsi già da piccoli e si snodano poi per una vita intera nonostante lontananza e, spesso, equivoci.<br />Un libro “breve” ed intenso sulla giovinezza ormai passata e sugli immancabili bilanci della vita su cui prima o poi ci si deve cimentare.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14198962920231944765">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_847188945">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847188945" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/14977150-kimmie" class="left imgcol" title="Kimmie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1354071068p2/14977150.jpg" alt="Kimmie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/847188945?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/14977150-kimmie" class="user" title="Kimmie">Kimmie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/14977150-kimmie?shelf=borrowed-books" class="actionLinkLite">borrowed-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/14977150-kimmie?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer847188945">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3651606064674090103">For the past several months, I have been inundated between work and school. My devotion to reading a book a week has been completely crushed as a result. <u>Bleachers</u> appeared to be light and refreshing, so I picked this book from my office library in hopes I could find a few occasional moments to sink into another world, forgetting all the stress around me. But I was most definitely wrong. Characters are driven by stereotypes and lack any type of depth, and the story is flat at best. <br /><br />I understand</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3651606064674090103">For the past several months, I have been inundated between work and school. My devotion to reading a book a week has been completely crushed as a result. <u>Bleachers</u> appeared to be light and refreshing, so I picked this book from my office library in hopes I could find a few occasional moments to sink into another world, forgetting all the stress around me. But I was most definitely wrong. Characters are driven by stereotypes and lack any type of depth, and the story is flat at best. <br /><br />I understand Grisham's purpose with this novel. Ideas of maintaining love/hate relationships and battling a lifetime of guilt for one's misdeeds are concepts most people can relate to. Perhaps the ending to this book will give you the solace you need.<br /><br /><u>Bleachers</u> was not entirely a lost cause. At least I learned football terminology that may impress my fiance. I feel a bit more prepared for next football season.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3651606064674090103">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/23858941-sam-schoenick" class="user" title="Sam Schoenick">Sam Schoenick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1447712404">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14580697336926769497">Personal Response: I really enjoyed <em>Bleachers</em> by John Grisham. It is my favorite book so far this year. I like how he described the relationships between characters. Character description was also very good and easy to visualize. Everything is very easy to follow along with.<br /><br />Plot: This book is all about a small town and its connection to football. Messina lives and dies for Spartan football. The town would be nothing without football. Eddie Rake who is the coach is about to die from cancer.This i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14580697336926769497">Personal Response: I really enjoyed <em>Bleachers</em> by John Grisham. It is my favorite book so far this year. I like how he described the relationships between characters. Character description was also very good and easy to visualize. Everything is very easy to follow along with.<br /><br />Plot: This book is all about a small town and its connection to football. Messina lives and dies for Spartan football. The town would be nothing without football. Eddie Rake who is the coach is about to die from cancer.This is a small town and this brought the town even closer together. Rake has set records for just about everything a coach can set a record for. When Neely Crenshaw finds out his coach is about to pass away he comes back to visit. Neely has not been to Messina since he had his jersey retired. Neely and Eddie Rake never had a great relationship. Crenshaw realizes how important of an influence Coach Rake is on him. Neely visits a lot of former teammates. He also comes back to meet his high school crush, Cameron. Neely says she is the only girl he has ever loved. Neely is the best quarterback to ever play at Messina. The town worships Neely Crenshaw and all of his accomplishments. Many thought Neely was going to win the Heisman trophy in college. Neely got injured in a game and it ended his football career. Once Coach Rake finally passes away, the town has a funeral for him at the football field. Neely has to give a eulogy about his coach, even though they did not have a great relationship. Neely realizes how much he actually loves Coach Rake, and how important he is to all of his players.<br /><br />Characterization: The main character of this book is Neely Crenshaw. He is a former quarterback for the Messina Spartans. All of the townspeople believe that he is the best quarterback to play for Messina. Neely is a tall gentlemen and very fit. Many townspeople look up to him as an idol. There are many other characters in this book. Some other main characters are Eddie Rake, Silo, Nat, and Cameron. Coach Rake influenced many people in his lifetime most of them were boys. Those boys will always have someone to look up to.<br /><br />Setting: The setting takes place in a small town in Texas, called Messina. The time is in the early 2000s. The setting is very important because of how close everyone is in Messina. If it took place in a large city people would not be as close to each other.<br /><br />Thematic Connection: The theme of this story is to never forget about the people who make a strong influence on you. You should never hold a grudge over someone who did so much for you. Neely held a grudge against Coach Rake his whole life. Never forget the past, because you can have so many memories you will never get to do again. Always remember where you come from.<br /><br />Recommendation: I would recommend this book to anybody that has ever played high school football. Boys can learn a lot of things from this story on how to never give up. This book is mostly for males in my opinion due to the sport. I would give this book a star rating of five.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14580697336926769497">...more</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1341152818">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1432993561120478398">For some reason this book was on my bookcase! I don't remember buying it and I don't think anyone gave it me as a gift but there it was... So, I thought I'd give it a go, mainly because I thought it would be interesting to compare to the Art of Fielding, another sports centred book by an American author.<br /><br />The advantage of this book over the Art of Fielding is that it is a lot shorter. This is even more fortunate as to be honest very little happens so if the book was longer it might get boring. The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1432993561120478398">For some reason this book was on my bookcase! I don't remember buying it and I don't think anyone gave it me as a gift but there it was... So, I thought I'd give it a go, mainly because I thought it would be interesting to compare to the Art of Fielding, another sports centred book by an American author.<br /><br />The advantage of this book over the Art of Fielding is that it is a lot shorter. This is even more fortunate as to be honest very little happens so if the book was longer it might get boring. The story focusses on the coming together of a small town's residents to mourn the death of a controversial American football coach who had put their home on the map.<br /><br />It was interesting to note the similar importance placed on sports success at American high schools. The kids on the team are revered almost as gods, with their photos adorning the walls of the local diner. The fact that the same is true of The Art of Fielding suggests this may be at least partially accurate. <br /><br />The lead character (apart from the terminally ill coach) is a former team hero whose career was wrecked young following a nasty injury. We watch him fight his demons to come to terms with events from his past all brought to a head by the death of Coach.<br /><br />An OK book, easy to read and quite short. However, I couldnt' really identify with any of the scenarios or characters in this book and as such I'm not sure if I would recommend it.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3128935764832242974">I like Grisham's stories (most of them), and while I am not a fan of football, I really liked this story. A legendary high school coach is dying, and his players from the past 44 years return home in his honor. For Neely Krenshaw, the return is particularly painful. <span id="freeTextContainer15467737291457351581"> Bleachers by John Grisham was about an all-American high school quarterback named Neely Crenshaw. He had played football at Messina high school and had gone on to play college football. After getting a hit to the knee, he was injured and couldn't play another game. After being hurt he swore never to come back to his home town, where he had been a legend. Fifteen years had past and learning that his high school football coach, Eddie Rake, was critically ill and would be gone soon, he had to brea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15467737291457351581"> Bleachers by John Grisham was about an all-American high school quarterback named Neely Crenshaw. He had played football at Messina high school and had gone on to play college football. After getting a hit to the knee, he was injured and couldn't play another game. After being hurt he swore never to come back to his home town, where he had been a legend. Fifteen years had past and learning that his high school football coach, Eddie Rake, was critically ill and would be gone soon, he had to break his promise to say goodbye. There was another reason that was known by only Neely and his team for him being gone all those years. When he arrives at the field, now called Rake Field in honor of their coach, he finds his old teammates. As they sit in the bleachers and wait for the stadiums lights to go out, symbolizing Rake has past, they drink beer and remember old times when they were an unstoppable team. One of the teammates found a tape of their most famous game. As they listen to the tape, Neely reveals the secret that has been kept for almost twenty years. What is it and why has it been buried until Coach Rake is almost buried himself?<br /> I liked that it was a book by my favorite author. John Grisham has been my favorite author for a few years and I have read and want to read lots of his books. I also liked that it was about sports. Football is one of my favorite sports, beside hunting and fishing, so I could picture the plays in my head when they were going through the games. There were lots of good things about this book, but the best was that you always had to keep guessing what would happen. The "secret" was talked about in the beginning of the book, but it wasn't revealed until the very end. One thing I disliked was the fact that it didn't talk about what happened to Neely and his friends after the funeral. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1367371067">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367371067" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45942174-ethan" class="left imgcol" title="Ethan"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Ethan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1367371067?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45942174-ethan" class="user" title="Ethan">Ethan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer1367371067'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1367371067">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2082046114730821284"> Bleachers was really a great read to me. If you love the sports genre, this book is great. It is about the Messina football legacy that Eddie Rake, an extremist football coach has left behind with his passing. With this occasion, his former players come together to relive and ponder what Coach Rake was really like. This book was definitely an easy read and really went into great depths of their high school football past. <br /><br /> "When you're famous at eighteen, you spend the rest of your life fading a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2082046114730821284">	Bleachers was really a great read to me. If you love the sports genre, this book is great. It is about the Messina football legacy that Eddie Rake, an extremist football coach has left behind with his passing. With this occasion, his former players come together to relive and ponder what Coach Rake was really like. This book was definitely an easy read and really went into great depths of their high school football past. <br /><br />	"When you're famous at eighteen, you spend the rest of your life fading away" (Grisham 188, Print).<br /><br />	Neely Crenshaw was the high school jock at the time while he was playing at Messina. He had everything he could ever want. Starting quarterback. One of the hottest girls in all of the school. Respect from everyone in the school. He was a very talented quarterback who could run the ball and toss it far and accurately. So with this talent he was drafted to Tech (a fictional school) for a large amount of money. In his sophomore year, he had a career ending knee injury that made him drop out of college. With this being said, he faded away into a nobody. He returned to Messina for the passing of his coach and very little people recognized him. Even though he had everything that made him great at a young age, he had last all of it later and became a nobody that wasn't cared about. He realized that the mistakes he made at his high school level really didn't set him up to have a great identity. He hurt others feelings, he didn't care for his future and that's why his personality was forgotten by many except for his close friends. Some of his close friends really remembered him for the bad things he had done too. Grisham portrayed the bad and good parts of his identity very well throughout the book and also the people around him. <br /><br />	This book was a great book to me. I would recommend this to sports fans and also to people who like character tales. John Grisham's ability to display detail comes out very well in this book. Slowly but surely, my dislike for reading is disappearing and I'm starting to enjoy many different styles of books. But again, I would definitely recommend this to anyone as it is one of my favorites. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2082046114730821284">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_44377825">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44377825" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1956885-jeff-cyrus" class="left imgcol" title="Jeff Cyrus"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Jeff Cyrus" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/44377825?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1956885-jeff-cyrus" class="user" title="Jeff Cyrus">Jeff Cyrus</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6024249-bleachers" title="Hardcover 9781417645657" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer44377825">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13805537521372841096"> Bleachers, by John Grisham, is about high school football in the town of Messina and their legendary coach, Eddie Rake. The town worships the football program because of this coach, to the point where the football booster club has more money than the school itself. In his years as head coach, the team won 13 state titles and over 400 games, including a winning streak that lasted six years and 84 wins. Neely Crenshaw was one of the star quarterbacks under Rake, so good that his number was retire</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13805537521372841096"> Bleachers, by John Grisham, is about high school football in the town of Messina and their legendary coach, Eddie Rake. The town worships the football program because of this coach, to the point where the football booster club has more money than the school itself. In his years as head coach, the team won 13 state titles and over 400 games, including a winning streak that lasted six years and 84 wins. Neely Crenshaw was one of the star quarterbacks under Rake, so good that his number was retired. When his NFL hopes were shattered from a cheap shot while playing college ball, Neely’s life does not have much meaning. <br />When he receives word that Coach Rake is ill and will soon pass away, Neely travels home to Messina, where he had not been in over ten years. He meets up with other players at night in the bleachers of Rake Field, where they used to play, and they sit and remember days of glory under Rake as they wait for him to die. Players from all different years under Rake’s rule show up, a rule that lasted thirty-four years. They all recall their own stories from their days of powerhouse football as they wait for the stadium lights to go out signifying the death of their famous coach. Neely must figure out whether he loved or hated Rake after years of stardom as a high school football star. He learns many lessons as he recalls the days under Rake, and as he tries to get his ex-girlfriend to forgive him from events that took place in high school. <br />	This is a book for all readers, as it covers many topics of life and touches on the importance of life lessons. Grisham uses a lot of dialogue in this novel, which at first is hard to follow, but gets easier and is quite enjoyable as you keep reading. This book is not all about football, though the characters share a commonality of playing under the same coach, and they often are found replaying the games from their high school careers. Grisham does not use a highly advanced vocabulary, making the book a somewhat easy read, and also a fun read. Grisham’s style of presenting the story makes you want to keep reading and find out how everything turns out in the end. <br />Readers will not be disappointed with the story, or with Grisham’s style of writing. A compelling story really makes you take a step back and evaluate your own life where it is now. Reading Bleachers can help you make your life better, and remind you that life is not all about fame and stardom, but is about being happy and enjoying what you have and making the best of things. If you want a good read that will help you in life, this is a good book for you. <br />I enjoyed reading this book and I am a big fan of Grisham. I like his writing style and they way he keeps you focused on the book and doesn’t let you stray from the storyline. I learned valuable life lessons while reading Bleachers. For example, I was reminded to always enjoy what I am doing and also never forget that I need to constantly evaluate where my life is at and where I would like it to be. When I finished reading this book, I wanted to read more of what Grisham has produced. I have heard many good things about Grisham and I can only back them up and say the same. The book is very interesting and it flows really well as you read. Out of ten, I would rate the book an eight. I highly recommend it for all readers because it captures football fans and also people who just like to read. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13805537521372841096">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17298757195081827428">Jonathan Boyer<br /><br />Mrs. Baltz<br /><br />Pre AP English 10<br /><br />12 December 2008<br /><br />Bleachers by John Grisham<br /><br />If you gave ever watched a high school football game, then you will know how they are filled with intense moments and not so intense ones. For coach Eddie Rake his life has been dedicated to high school football and some what reflects some of the high intensity moments and the not so intense moments. Author John Grisham gives you a look at a small southern town in a crisis as there most favored coach lies on his de</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17298757195081827428">Jonathan Boyer<br /><br />Mrs. Baltz<br /><br />Pre AP English 10<br /><br />12 December 2008<br /><br />Bleachers by John Grisham<br /><br />If you gave ever watched a high school football game, then you will know how they are filled with intense moments and not so intense ones. For coach Eddie Rake his life has been dedicated to high school football and some what reflects some of the high intensity moments and the not so intense moments. Author John Grisham gives you a look at a small southern town in a crisis as there most favored coach lies on his death bed.<br /><br /><br />	Neely Crenshaw was an all American quarter back and was destined for fame. When in a game near the end of his high school career and getting ready for a collage team position when he was hit late in a play that severely messed up his right knee. After the hit and his career were over Neely moved away to another town. Neely was confused on if he liked Coach Rake or if he should hate him. After receiving news that his old coach is on his brink with death he returns to the town of Messina. Upon his return news spread quick of the once all American being back. The little town becomes very delighted to see him. While every were he goes he finds someone who knows him he cant get coach of his mind.<br /><br />	The little town on Messina revolves around foot ball. When coach Eddie is hospitalized and a new coach takes his place things get really bad. The messina Spartans suffer from a losing season. This season is also the first in the schools history that the Spartans wont be going to the play offs. For the new coach he has to endure the humility and take the blame for the losing season.<br /><br />	Coach Eddie Rake is a do things his way kind of guy. Coach has no real plans he just does it and usually succeeds. Coach can make his self look like a real good guy and then he can make you angrier than you have ever been. Coach had a personality all to his self. One day he acted like he was just the world’s most jolly person then the next he would be angrier than a bull. <br /><br />	 Neely is a guy you can get along with and is very out going. He is a grudge holder kind of person to. When neely gets hurt he holds everyone responsible but him self. Thus being his reason for moving away and not knowing if he should for give coach or hate him. While Neely sits on the old bleachers at the football field he sits and talks to some old friends. The lights around the field stay on during the night to signal that Eddie is still with them. When the lights go off it signals that Eddie has passed away. Now as Neely sits under the lights he has too make one of his biggest decisions. Will he forgive eddies or keep this grudge.<br /><br /><br />	The overall theme of this story is to not run away form your problems. If you have some problems no matter what size it can be worked out. This book I would recommend it to people who like sports and drama. I personally did not like this book and would not recommend it to someone who doesn’t like a lot of drama. <br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer144682515">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17506698238125084977">It's a good thing this book was a quick read otherwise I wouldn't have bothered finishing it. This book is about a man living in the past and yearning for the glory days as a high school football star. His old coach is dying and the players he's coached for decades return home to hold vigil until his death.<br /><br />I found it all quite sad. The love/hate relationship each of the players have/had with the abusive coach have had a huge impact on their lives. There were so many questions running through my</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17506698238125084977">It's a good thing this book was a quick read otherwise I wouldn't have bothered finishing it. This book is about a man living in the past and yearning for the glory days as a high school football star. His old coach is dying and the players he's coached for decades return home to hold vigil until his death.<br /><br />I found it all quite sad. The love/hate relationship each of the players have/had with the abusive coach have had a huge impact on their lives. There were so many questions running through my head while reading this book: Where were the parents of these guys when this was going on? Why would you live your life trying to live up to the standards of such a bully much less take the time to attend his funeral? When will these men grow up and move on? Why is an entire town so mesmerized by high school football?<br /><br />Yes, I "get" the yearning for the fun and glory of youth. I understand regrets for mistakes made in the past, loves lost, etc. <br /><br />While the writing is picturesque the subject is less than riviting. I much prefer Grisham's legal thrillers. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17506698238125084977">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/80600274?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 10, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2773310-robin" class="user" title="Robin">Robin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer80600274">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13623673769055716205">Definitely not what I expected from John Grisham. I went through my "Grisham phase" years ago, loving The Firm, The Pelican Brief, etc, but stopped reading when it seemed like I kept reading the same book over and over-if it ain't broke, don't fix it. I found Bleachers on my son's bookcase (he read it for a high school book report) and figured it would be a quick read. It was - I finished it in one night. It was a predictable story of a high school football program and it's former hard-nosed, ne</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13623673769055716205">Definitely not what I expected from John Grisham. I went through my "Grisham phase" years ago, loving The Firm, The Pelican Brief, etc, but stopped reading when it seemed like I kept reading the same book over and over-if it ain't broke, don't fix it. I found Bleachers on my son's bookcase (he read it for a high school book report) and figured it would be a quick read. It was - I finished it in one night. It was a predictable story of a high school football program and it's former hard-nosed, never-say-quit, win-at-all-costs but now dying coach, told from the point of view of the prototypical star quarterback who blew out his knee in college and never fully recovered physically or emotionally. Former players gravitate back to town to sit in vigil on the bleachers of the football field and relive their individual glory days and those of the team throughout the years. If you're looking for action, you won't find it here. What you will find is many stories of one man who touched the lives of an entire community, for better and worse.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13623673769055716205">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_70760016">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70760016" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2723599-chad-sayban" class="left imgcol" title="Chad Sayban"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1333320931p2/2723599.jpg" alt="Chad Sayban" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/70760016?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2723599-chad-sayban" class="user" title="Chad Sayban">Chad Sayban</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=good" class="actionLinkLite">good</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=home-library" class="actionLinkLite">home-library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer70760016">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9607071329530723635">There is no doubt that Bleachers is not your typical John Grisham book. There is no legal intrigue. There are no courtroom heroics. Nobody is murdered. However, there is a good story here. At 163 pages, this book is closer to a novella than to a novel in length. I read the entire story in one day (I know, pretty lame) and it was a fun read. The story revolves around the return of football star Neely Crenshaw to his home town because of the impending death of his football coach Eddie Rake. Coach</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9607071329530723635">There is no doubt that Bleachers is not your typical John Grisham book. There is no legal intrigue. There are no courtroom heroics. Nobody is murdered. However, there is a good story here. At 163 pages, this book is closer to a novella than to a novel in length. I read the entire story in one day (I know, pretty lame) and it was a fun read. The story revolves around the return of football star Neely Crenshaw to his home town because of the impending death of his football coach Eddie Rake. Coach Rake made himself a town legend, but a controversial legend to be sure. Players from generations of teams migrate back to the field they played on – each for their own reason - to tell stories of their time in the program, both good and bad. Some see Rake as a hero while others can’t shake the man’s obvious flaws. But the real story is Neely trying to come to grips with his relationship with Rake – whether to hate him or respect him and the ‘incident’ kept a secret for 15 years – and the town’s reverence for both Rake and Neely over a ‘silly game.’ The book shines a light on the way sports can become far more than just sport and how people come to grips with their past when they are forced to come back to it. I think Grisham was wise to have written the story as such a short piece. It would have dragged if he attempted to turn it into a 350-page novel. But as it stands, it is a quick, fun read and I really enjoyed characters and the story.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9607071329530723635">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer334904544">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer112871995688604539"><strong>Change of pace for Grisham</strong><br /><br /><em>Read by John Grisham<br />4 hours, 22 minutes</em><br /><br />I, for one, am not especially enamored of Grisham's legal thrillers but I did enjoy Grisham's foray into non-legal fiction.<br /><br />Bleachers was read by the author. Grisham's southern accent and good ol' boy style are sometimes helpful but his occasional odd emphasis and flat read can be distracting.<br /><br />The book features a Bobby Knight/Woody Hayes type of small-town high school football coach. He is cruel, petty and completely breaks his playe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText112871995688604539"><strong>Change of pace for Grisham</strong><br /><br /><em>Read by John Grisham<br />4 hours, 22 minutes</em><br /><br />I, for one, am not especially enamored of Grisham's legal thrillers but I did enjoy Grisham's foray into non-legal fiction.<br /><br />Bleachers was read by the author. Grisham's southern accent and good ol' boy style are sometimes helpful but his occasional odd emphasis and flat read can be distracting.<br /><br />The book features a Bobby Knight/Woody Hayes type of small-town high school football coach. He is cruel, petty and completely breaks his players as he builds them into his mold and makes them successful teams year after year after year. His teams have won 13 Texas state championships.<br /><br />The coach is dying of cancer now and his players are returning home to honor him and await his funeral. They meet several times on the bleachers of the field they played on and discuss their memories of school, football and of course the coach. Thus, the title.<br /><br />We see the reunion of players through the eyes of Neeley, a former All-American quarterback who suffered a career-ending injury in college and never reached his full potential as a player. Although Neeley is our window to this world, he is not the true focus of the book - it is the coach and the love/hate relationship his players and the town have with him.<br /><br />An interesting book. This Indiana University graduate couldn't help but wonder if the alumni of Bobby Knight's basketball program have similar discussions about him.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://dwdsreviews.blogspot.ca/2011/07/bleachers-audiobook-by-john-grisham.html" target="_blank">http://dwdsreviews.blogspot.ca/2011/0...</a></span>

      <a href="/user/show/3901425-jerry" class="user" title="Jerry">Jerry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer112588787">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13804528197459189610"> Poignant and emotional, but plotless and somewhat boring...<br /><br />We wonder if this little hardback about little more than small-town high school football is somewhat autobiographical, given that the dust jacket mentions that for a while Grisham quarterbacked the Southaven High (Miss.) team? Like "A Painted House", this book is not about lawyers, and is definitely not a thriller. Rather it is a nostalgic look back at a group of boys who played football for a notorious love/hate-type coach, Eddie Rake.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13804528197459189610"> Poignant and emotional, but plotless and somewhat boring...<br /><br />We wonder if this little hardback about little more than small-town high school football is somewhat autobiographical, given that the dust jacket mentions that for a while Grisham quarterbacked the Southaven High (Miss.) team? Like "A Painted House", this book is not about lawyers, and is definitely not a thriller. Rather it is a nostalgic look back at a group of boys who played football for a notorious love/hate-type coach, Eddie Rake. Rake is dying of cancer and many of the boys, some of whom still live in town, convene a vigil at Rake Field and sit on the bleachers to reminisce. That's about it. While at times the book showed insight and emotion, at others it was dull and plodding. An attempt by the central character (Neely Crenshaw, the old QB) to redeem a former love affair gone awry was pretty silly, and thankfully for the women, the girl tolerated no parts of it.<br /><br />Anything Grisham writes, including this novella, will no doubt sell a bazillion copies. This quick read might just as well be checked out from the library if you insist. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13804528197459189610">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48645299?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 08, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1458236-jaime" class="user" title="Jaime">Jaime</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48645299">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17773812963774183716">The title of my book is Bleachers. With this novel author John Grisham showed us he could write something other than a boring legal drama. I had read some of his other works such as The Firm, The Pelican Brief, A time to Kill, and The Runaway Jury and Bleachers was unlike any of them. The story tells about a high school football dynasty in Mississippi through the eyes of former all-state quarterback Neely Crenshaw. It talks about the people of the town and how life revolved around football. For</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17773812963774183716">The title of my book is Bleachers. With this novel author John Grisham showed us he could write something other than a boring legal drama. I had read some of his other works such as The Firm, The Pelican Brief, A time to Kill, and The Runaway Jury and Bleachers was unlike any of them. The story tells about a high school football dynasty in Mississippi through the eyes of former all-state quarterback Neely Crenshaw. It talks about the people of the town and how life revolved around football. For Neely looking back on those days wasn't so pleasant. The thought of football just reminded his of the huge stress he was under when he played for the Messina Spartans. He was always afraid of failing in a town so obsessed with football, and under a coach who was always extremely hard on him since the first time he stepped foot in Messina High's field house. I think Mr. Grisham must have played a little ball in his day because the play by play in the book is so vivid and descriptive. I could almost see the plays unfold as i read. For being such a different genre than im used to reading from John Grisham i thought it was good. I like reading sports related books ajnd this book is by far my favorite. Not only did i think the play by play was good but it reminded me of my playing days when i was a boy. I guess i liked it alot because i could relate to the story, and i would recommend it to anyone who is into sports related novels. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17773812963774183716">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_59335876">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59335876" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/951731-dlora" class="left imgcol" title="Dlora"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1204265002p2/951731.jpg" alt="Dlora" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/59335876?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 12, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/951731-dlora" class="user" title="Dlora">Dlora</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5347.Bleachers" title="Paperback 9780099468196" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/951731-dlora?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer59335876">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18087105162781866860">I have read <em>Bleachers</em> before but I had a yen to read it again. I appreciated it even more the second time around. I was intrigued with how Grisham handled his narrative. Unlike his legal thrillers or his more recent soapbox-message novels, this story is about a legendary football coach in the small live-for-football town of Messina. Coach Rake is dying and all his football players from his long years of coaching are gathering for the funeral, including All-American Neely Crenshaw, one of Coach R</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18087105162781866860">I have read <em>Bleachers</em> before but I had a yen to read it again. I appreciated it even more the second time around. I was intrigued with how Grisham handled his narrative. Unlike his legal thrillers or his more recent soapbox-message novels, this story is about a legendary football coach in the small live-for-football town of Messina. Coach Rake is dying and all his football players from his long years of coaching are gathering for the funeral, including All-American Neely Crenshaw, one of Coach Rake's most famous quarterbacks. Neely obviously has held a grudge against his coach for fifteen years, and as the players reminisce and relive their high school glory days, we slowly and almost with suspense discover what happened between the coach and his boys in the last state championship game. We see the players decide if they love or hate the powerful Coach Rake, and we get to make the same decision as we read along. Is he a good guy or a bad guy? Is football an overrated, dangerous game? Does it undermine the character and morals of young teens to be a football hero during high school or make them better prepared to live life? I'm not a football fan but I really enjoyed this novel; it's more about relationships than it is about football. I think it is one of Grisham's best novels.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18087105162781866860">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10887708759387557228">This book really surprised me! I did not want to stop reading. And I don´t really know what it was that I liked about it, maybe it was the team spirit and the going back and reliving the adolescent years and meeting those people from that time. Not much happened, but I liked it. I do not know about American football. And to make me like a book like this, means the author must be good. It´s been years since I last read a Grisham book. I really need to read more again.<br /><br /><br /><br />Tuesday-Wednesday<br /><br />Strange how this books is feeling like a good one, when nothing really happens in it, it´s just reminiscing. So an american football coach is dying and all these old trainees of his are gathering in town, remembering the times when they played. I´m still amazed by how good this book is. I don´t understand much about American football, I´ve never seen a whole game. But I just keep reading more and more. Strange how some books are like that, really good even if you can´t explain what´s good about it!<br /><br />Thursday-the End<br /><br />Maybe it´s the team spirit. And the whole re-living the adolescent years by meeting those same people and talking about those times.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_258055781">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258055781" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7364648-andrew" class="left imgcol" title="Andrew"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1325982265p2/7364648.jpg" alt="Andrew" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/258055781?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7364648-andrew" class="user" title="Andrew">Andrew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8151326-bleachers" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer258055781">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7855230441944125247">In my mind, this book stands apart from the other John Grisham novels that I have read. Those that focus on the legal world tended to hurtle along at break-neck speed, following the lives of exceptional characters in Hollywood situations. I’m thinking first and foremost of <em>“The Firm”</em> here, which is the most re-read of all the books I own by the author.<br /><br />Bleachers is an entirely different prospect. The story is more reflective, as the characters look back and remember their past lives. I did enjoy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7855230441944125247">In my mind, this book stands apart from the other John Grisham novels that I have read. Those that focus on the legal world tended to hurtle along at break-neck speed, following the lives of exceptional characters in Hollywood situations. I’m thinking first and foremost of <em>“The Firm”</em> here, which is the most re-read of all the books I own by the author.<br /><br />Bleachers is an entirely different prospect. The story is more reflective, as the characters look back and remember their past lives. I did enjoy the book, partly because I love football, and partly because it evokes memories of meeting my own childhood friends, and reliving all our sporting memories of yesteryear. <br /><br />I struggled to relate to the star quarterback protagonist, and that was the main weakness of the book for me. Perhaps I might have felt more for the coach too, if I had grown up an American kid, and played sport in that sort of world. He takes on a “larger than life” role in the town, and that is unheard of for a high-school coach over here.<br /><br />By no means the best book I have ever read, and I’d struggle to accept it was “unforgettable”, but it’s an easy read that is worth picking up if you like football, or ever played for a sports team when you were younger.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7855230441944125247">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7698792954106405176">This book is great! First it talks about the city of Messina and how they are dedicated and love their high school team. Citizens in Messina respected Coach Rake so</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7698792954106405176">This book is great! First it talks about the city of Messina and how they are dedicated and love their high school team. They were the best in the country and how they had a long streak and they won the state championship and all. The city would be nothing without this famous highschool team. And this high school team had a famous coach named Eddie Rake which. He would push the players really hard and he was very strict and made the players run miles. Citizens in Messina respected Coach Rake so much they even named their stadium the Rake Field. But this was the past. After a lot of years that past, former players started meaning at Rake Field, but the author didn't tell why. But then you will figure out that Eddie Rake was about to die, so the former players were waiting. It was emotional process and the whole book was from the perspective of a former player named Neely. He tells us the past and the successful football team and how Coach Rake got fired! This book is very interesting and you should read this if you are a fan of football<br /></span>

A Pulitzer Prize-winner for his ground-breaking reporting on the Vietnam War, Halberstam wrote more than 20 books, almost all of them bestsellers. His work has stood the test of time and has become the standard by which all journalists measure themselves.The Teammates is the profoundly moving story of four great baseball players who have made the passage from sports icons--when they were young and seemingly indestructible--to men dealing with the vulnerabilities of growing older. At the core of the book is the friendship of these four very different men--Boston Red Sox teammates Bobby Doerr, Dominic DiMaggio, Johnny Pesky, and Ted Williams--who remained close for more than sixty years.The book starts out in early October 2001, when Dominic DiMaggio and Johnny Pesky begin a 1,300-mile trip by car to visit their beloved friend Ted Williams, whom they know is dying. Bobby Doerr, the fourth member of this close group--&amp;quot;my guys,&amp;quot; Williams used to call them--is unable to join them.This is a book--filled with historical details and first-hand
